The described changes\\n25: // are not applied directly, but contain an approximation of the final\\n26: // result that will be completed during apply by resolving any values that\\n27: // cannot be predicted.\\n28: //\\n29: // A plan must always be accompanied by the configuration it was built from,\\n30: // since the plan does not itself include all of the information required to\\n31: // make the changes indicated.\\n32: type Plan struct {\\n33: \\t// Mode is the mode under which this plan was created.\\n34: \\t//\\n35: \\t// This is only recorded to allow for UI differences when presenting plans\\n36: \\t// to the end-user, and so it must not be used to influence apply-time\\n37: \\t// behavior. VariableValues can potentially contain\\n53: \\t// unknown values for a speculative plan, but the variable values must\\n54: \\t// all be known for a plan that will subsequently be applied.\\n55: \\t//\\n56: \\t// ApplyTimeVariables retains the names of any ephemeral variables that were\\n57: \\t// set (non-null) during the planning phase and must therefore be\\n58: \\t// re-supplied by the caller (potentially with different values) during\\n59: \\t// the apply phase. Ephemeral input variables are intended for populating\\n60: \\t// arguments for other ephemeral objects in the configuration, such as\\n61: \\t// provider configurations. If not then the plan was created successfully but found\\n95: \\t// no material differences between desired and prior state, and so\\n96: \\t// applying this plan would achieve nothing.\\n97: \\tApplyable bool\\n98: \\n99: \\t// Errored is true if the Changes information is incomplete because\\n100: \\t// the planning operation failed. An errored plan cannot be applied,\\n101: \\t// but can be cautiously inspected for debugging purposes.\\n102: \\tErrored bool\\n103: \\n104: \\t// Checks captures a snapshot of the (probably-incomplete) check results\\n105: \\t// at the end of the planning process.\\n106: \\t//\\n107: \\t// If this plan is applyable (that is, if the planning process completed\\n108: \\t// without errors) then the set of checks here should be complete even\\n109: \\t// though some of them will likely have StatusUnknown where the check\\n110: \\t// condition depends on values we won't know until the apply step.\\n111: \\tChecks *states.CheckResults\\n112: \\n113: \\t// RelevantAttributes is a set of resource instance addresses and\\n114: \\t// attributes that are either directly affected by proposed changes or may\\n115: \\t// have indirectly contributed to them via references in expressions.\\n116: \\t//\\n117: \\t// This is the result of a heuristic and is intended only as a hint to\\n118: \\t// the UI layer in case it wants to emphasize or de-emphasize certain\\n119: \\t// resources. Don't use this to drive any non-cosmetic behavior, especially\\n120: \\t// including anything that would be subject to compatibility constraints.\\n121: \\tRelevantAttributes []globalref.ResourceAttr\\n122: \\n123: \\t// PrevRunState and PriorState both describe the situation that the plan\\n124: \\t// was derived from:\\n125: \\t//\\n126: \\t// PrevRunState is a representation of the outcome of the previous\\n127: \\t// Terraform operation, without any updates from the remote system but\\n128: \\t// potentially including some changes that resulted from state upgrade\\n129: \\t// actions.\\n130: \\t//\\n131: \\t// PriorState is a representation of the current state of remote objects,\\n132: \\t// which will differ from PrevRunState if the \\\"refresh\\\" step returned\\n133: \\t// different data, which might reflect drift.\\n134: \\t//\\n135: \\t// PriorState is the main snapshot we use for actions during apply.\\n136: \\t// PrevRunState is only here so that we can diff PriorState against it in\\n137: \\t// order to report to the user any out-of-band changes we've detected.\\n138: \\tPrevRunState *states.State\\n139: \\tPriorState   *states.State\\n140: \\n141: \\t// ExternalReferences are references that are being made to resources within\\n142: \\t// the plan from external sources.\\n143: \\t//\\n144: \\t// This is never recorded outside of Terraform. It is not written into the\\n145: \\t// binary plan file, and it is not written into the JSON structured outputs.\\n146: \\t// The testing framework never writes the plans out but holds everything in\\n147: \\t// memory as it executes, so there is no need to add any kind of\\n148: \\t// serialization for this field. This does mean that you shouldn't rely on\\n149: \\t// this field existing unless you have just generated the plan.\\n150: \\tExternalReferences []*addrs.Reference\\n151: \\n152: \\t// Overrides contains the set of overrides that were applied while making\\n153: \\t// this plan. We need to provide the same set of overrides when applying\\n154: \\t// the plan so we preserve them here. *mocking.Overrides\\n158: \\n159: \\t// Timestamp is the record of truth for when the plan happened.\\n160: \\tTimestamp time.Time\\n161: \\n162: \\t// ProviderFunctionResults stores hashed results from all provider\\n163: \\t// function calls, so that calls during apply can be checked for\\n164: \\t// consistency.\\n165: \\tProviderFunctionResults []providers.FunctionHash\\n166: }\\n167: \\n168: // ProviderAddrs returns a list of all of the provider configuration addresses\\n169: // referenced throughout the receiving plan.\\n170: //\\n171: // The result is de-duplicated so that each distinct address appears only once.\\n172: func (p *Plan) ProviderAddrs() []addrs.AbsProviderConfig {\\n173: \\tif p == nil || p.Changes == nil {\\n174: \\t\\treturn nil\\n175: \\t}\\n176: \\n177: \\t\\tkeys = append(keys, k)\\n189: \\t}\\n190: \\tsort.Strings(keys)\\n191: \\n192: \\tret := make([]addrs.AbsProviderConfig, len(keys))\\n193: \\tfor i, key := range keys {\\n194: \\t\\tret[i] = m[key]\\n195: \\t}\\n196: \\n197: \\treturn ret\\n198: }\\n199: \\n200: // Backend represents the backend-related configuration and other data as it\\n201: // existed when a plan was created.\\n202: type Backend struct {\\n203: \\t// Type is the type of backend that the plan will apply against.\\n204: \\tType string\\n205: \\n206: \\t// Config is the configuration of the backend, whose schema is Don't use this to drive any non-cosmetic behavior, especially\\n120: \\t// including anything that would be subject to compatibility constraints.\\n121: \\tRelevantAttributes []globalref.ResourceAttr\\n122: \\n123: \\t// PrevRunState and PriorState both describe the situation that the plan\\n124: \\t// was derived from:\\n125: \\t//\\n126: \\t// PrevRunState is a representation of the outcome of the previous\\n127: \\t// Terraform operation, without any updates from the remote system but\\n128: \\t// potentially including some changes that resulted from state upgrade\\n129: \\t// actions.\\n130: \\t//\\n131: \\t// PriorState is a representation of the current state of remote objects,\\n132: \\t// which will differ from PrevRunState if the \\\"refresh\\\" step returned\\n133: \\t// different data, which might reflect drift.\\n134: \\t//\\n135: \\t// PriorState is the main snapshot we use for actions during apply.\\n136: \\t// PrevRunState is only here so that we can diff PriorState against it in\\n137: \\t// order to report to the user any out-of-band changes we've detected.\\n138: \\tPrevRunState *states.State\\n139: \\tPriorState   *states.State\\n140: \\n141: \\t// ExternalReferences are references that are being made to resources within\\n142: \\t// the plan from external sources.\\n143: \\t//\\n144: \\t// This is never recorded outside of Terraform. It is not written into the\\n145: \\t// binary plan file, and it is not written into the JSON structured outputs.\\n146: \\t// The testing framework never writes the plans out but holds everything in\\n147: \\t// memory as it executes, so there is no need to add any kind of\\n148: \\t// serialization for this field. This does mean that you shouldn't rely on\\n149: \\t// this field existing unless you have just generated the plan.\\n150: \\tExternalReferences []*addrs.Reference\\n151: \\n152: \\t// Overrides contains the set of overrides that were applied while making\\n153: \\t// this plan. We need to provide the same set of overrides when applying\\n154: \\t// the plan so we preserve them here. The described changes\n25: // are not applied directly, but contain an approximation of the final\n26: // result that will be completed during apply by resolving any values that\n27: // cannot be predicted.\n28: //\n29: // A plan must always be accompanied by the configuration it was built from,\n30: // since the plan does not itself include all of the information required to\n31: // make the changes indicated.\n32: type Plan struct {\n33: \t// Mode is the mode under which this plan was created.\n34: \t//\n35: \t// This is only recorded to allow for UI differences when presenting plans\n36: \t// to the end-user, and so it must not be used to influence apply-time\n37: \t// behavior. ResourceInstanceChange describes a change to a particular resource instance\n213: // object.\n214: type ResourceInstanceChange struct {\n215: \t// Addr is the absolute address of the resource instance that the change\n216: \t// will apply to.\n217: \tAddr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n218: \n219: \t// PrevRunAddr is the absolute address that this resource instance had at\n220: \t// the conclusion of a previous run.\n221: \t//\n222: \t// This will typically be the same as Addr, but can be different if the\n223: \t// previous resource instance was subject to a \"moved\" block that we\n224: \t// In that case, it's up to the codepath making that decision to\n261: \t// decide which value would provide the most relevant explanation to the\n262: \t// end-user and return that.  23→func (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {\n    24→\tif plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil {\n    25→\t\treturn \"\"\n    26→\t}\n    27→\n CompactDiffFormatter produces a condensed, summary-style diff output for\n// terraform plan, showing only resource-level changes without attribute-level detail.\ntype CompactDiffFormatter struct{}\n\n// Format returns a compact string representation of a plan's changes,\n// grouped by action type and showing only resource-level information.\nfunc (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {\n\tif plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil {\n\t\treturn \"\"\n\t}\n\n\t// Group resources by action\n\tresources := make(map[plans.Action][]*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc)\n\tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n\t\taction := rc.Action\n\t\tresources[action] = append(resources[action], rc)\n\t}\n\n\t// Sort each action's resources\n\tfor action := range resources {\n\t\tsort.Slice(resources[action], func(i, j int) bool {\n\t\t\treturn resources[action][i].Addr.String() < resources[action][j].Addr.String()\n\t\t})\n\t}\n\n\tvar buf bytes.Buffer\n\n\t// Define the order of actions to display\n\tactionOrder := []plans.Action{\n\t\tplans.Create,\n\t\tplans.Update,\n\t\tplans.Delete,\n\t\tplans.DeleteThenCreate,\n\t\tplans.CreateThenDelete,\n\t\tplans.Read,\n\t\tplans.NoOp,\n\t}\n\n\t// Output resources grouped by action\n\tfor _, action := range actionOrder {\n\t\tif len(resources[action]) == 0 {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Write action header with count\n\t\tactionSymbol := actionToSymbol(action)\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(fmt.Sprintf(\"[%s] %s (%d)\\n\", actionSymbol, actionToLabel(action), len(resources[action])))\n\n\t\t// Write each resource\n\t\tfor _, rc := range resources[action] {\n\t\t\tbuf.WriteString(fmt.Sprintf(\"  %s.%s\\n\", rc.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type, rc.Addr.Resource.Resource.Name))\n\n\t\t\t// Add instance key if present\n\t\t\tif
